        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1575294286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12074823462857875587"><b>1st Read:</b> January 2015<br/><b>2nd Read:</b> March 2016<br/><b>3rd Read:</b> March 2018<br/><b>4th Read:</b> Oct 2019<br/><br/><br/><b>Rereading In preparation for [Call Down The Hawk]</b><br/>Because of course I am. 😌 I've got to say, I don't usually reread a series so much and being immersed in the audiobook again is both comforting and heartaching (it's like missing an old friend) and fresh. Even now. I still notice little things and my heart just feels incredibly <i>full</i>. These characters have long since stopped being ink on paper.<br/><br/>my particularly favourite </span>
  <span id="freeText12074823462857875587" style="display:none"><b>1st Read:</b> January 2015<br /><b>2nd Read:</b> March 2016<br /><b>3rd Read:</b> March 2018<br /><b>4th Read:</b> Oct 2019<br /><br /><br /><b>Rereading In preparation for [Call Down The Hawk]</b><br />Because of course I am. 😌 I've got to say, I don't usually reread a series so much and being immersed in the audiobook again is both comforting and heartaching (it's like missing an old friend) and fresh. Even now. I still notice little things and my heart just feels incredibly <i>full</i>. These characters have long since stopped being ink on paper.<br /><br />my particularly favourite moments of this reread were:<br />Blue consuming only yogurt and using her illegal pink switch blade quite a lot. Also that time she tried to hit Noah for saying she had nice legs (that gas station scene tho omg). All of Ronan's aggressive attempts to take Adam on dates. ("You're doing this thing with me." "What?" Scene: They fight. Scene: they maybe nearly die. Scene: they plot murder. Later, Ronan: "a successful date.") And Gansey just having panic attacks because nothing is more relatable. <br /><br />----<br /><br />Idek how it's possibly...BUT I LOVE THIS BOOK EVEN <i>MORE</i> THIS TIME AND I ALREADY LOVED IT ASTRONOMICALLY SO THE FIRST TIME. *shrieks* The thing that most makes me sob in this series (apart from precious #Pynch moments) is the fact that <i>it makes me think so so much</i>. Like I have theories! I see little nuggets and clues! I just feel like I got SO SO MUCH MORE OUT OF IT THE SECOND TIME. And <i>everything</i> makes me want to hold it and shriek and cry basically. Everything. ADJFAKSLDF<br /><br /><b>Things I Appreciated During This Re-Read:</b><br />• Everything #Pynch.<br />• Realising Adam's INCREDIBLE character development...where he even admits his pride is an idiot.<br />• Realising Ronan's INCREDIBLE character development...he is not a drunk raging asshole so much anymore. Still nasty. But wonderful. But nasty. BUT WONDERFUL.<br />• The fact that the way the title is REPEATED probably is a nod to <b>Blue being a mirror</b>. Yes?? Yesss?? DO YOU THINK???<br />• I accidentally love the Gray Man. He is a good father to Blue. &lt;3<br />• PERSEPHONE. 3 *SHRIEKS*<br />• Gansey darling. His panic attack was the best thing in the world. Not because I want him to suffer but because GANSEY + ANXIETY = ADORABLE COOKIE POT WHOM IS RELATABLE AND I LOVE.<br />•I love Gansey.<br />• GANSEEEEY. <br />• #SaveGansey<br />• Blue's feminist fights were the best.<br />• Also Jesse Dittley. 3 *SHRIEKS MORE*<br />• Also is it just me or is Greenmantle like Metatron from Supernatural? Yes. Say yes basically.<br />• THIS SERIES FREAKING SPLITS ME IN HALF<b> AND I LOVE IT.</b> I CANNOT STOP THINKING ABOUT IT.<br />• I ACTUALLY FEEL LIKE RE-READING IT AGAIN IMMEDIATELY. WHAT'S WRONG WITH ME.<br />• How is this book so so good.<br />• I need a moment<br />• possibly nine moments.<br />• If I could only pick one favourite series...just ONE...it would be this one. I wouldn't even hesitate.<br />• DO YOU REALISE HOW MUCH I LOVE IT NOW?!?! OKAY. OKAY. I'M CALMING. Caaalming. <br />• I shall be over here, rocking gently and cry and waiting for The Raven King.<br /><br /><br />***<br /><br /><b>Here is my 2015 Review:</b><br /><br />I've put off reviewing this because I just feel ALL OF THE THINGS. And my reviews for these kinds of books never adequately sum up how much I love them. So...I LOVE THIS BOOK A LOT OKAY AND YOU SHOULD GO READ IT AND THERE IS NOTHING BETTER THAN A MAGGIE STIEFVATER BOOK AND I WILL LITERALLY BEG ON MY KNEES FOR THE FINAL BOOK THAT CLIFFHANGER WAS WICKED. GANSEEEEEY.<br /><br />I am a huge Maggie Stiefvater fan and basically give all her books 5-stars...so maybe i'm a little biased but THIS WAS AMAZINGLY FANtASTIC. I think The Raven Boys is still my favourite of the trilogy because it introduced me to these amazing characters. But the Dream Thieves broke my heart and Blue Lily Lily Blue just extended my craziness of passionate obsession for this series. <br /><br />Since it's the 3rd in a series, it's hard to review without spoilers. While The Dream Thieves was more about Ronan, this one is back to being more about Blue. Everyone makes great leaps and bounds in character development. Ronan will forever break my heart...and there was quite a few shippable Ronan/Adam moments. I'm not EXACTLY sure how I stand with my shipping. I want to ship ALL OF THE THINGS like the fangirl I am. But I'm also very aware that I want everything to stay the same with my Raven Boys And 1 Girl. I want their epic tight-knit group of friendship to just stay exactly the same. And once people start getting together, that all gets ruiend. And Gansey knows this, which is why he won't admit he likes Blue. Also the whole if-she-kisses-him-she'll-kill-him.<br /><br />Can I take a moment to say I'm FREAKING TERRIFIED FOR GANSEY?!! He's going to die. Blue predicted it in book 1. BUT I CAN'T HAVE GANSEY DIE. I've been with him for 3 books and I just love him more and more and he and Blue are adorable. They ring each other up in the middle of the night even thought it's "against the rules" (their own private rules of not liking each other) and they talk about birds or congress. Never each other. It is the sweetest most adorable relationship I've ever read. And I LOVE it. I love how different they are to typical YA books. <br /><br />I love how this book is book is focused on dead Welsh kings and FRIENDSHIP mostly...and then shippable things secondly. I really love books about friendship, okay?<br /><br />But let's talk a little about all the characters, shall we?! (Yes, yes we shall.)<br /><br />BLUE: She's as feisty but calm/sweet as ever. I love how Blue has such a huge personality but she's kind of serious and not prone to losing her mind over anything. She will not be belittled. She will stand up for herself. She's such a feminist and doesn't need a boy to save her. She's also short. I didn't actually realise till this book how short she is! BUT IT'S HILARIOUS. There are so many short-jokes.<br />GANSEY: I love Gansey. He is smooth and he keeps everyone together so well. But he has secrets...like a bit more comes out about his immense secrets in this book. For some reason Gansey seemed more boyish than usual. Like he's so collected al of the time...but....it's like death is closer and I AM FREAKING OUT OAKY?!!<br />ADAM: Is finally starting to grow a brain and he's whole mantra is "don't fight with Gansey don't fight with Blue" and I appreciate that. Adam is so tough and strong and he's so fragile. But I love him. He and Ronan fight something vicious but they are THERE for each other, which just gives me ajfdsklad feels. Even not as a couple. JUST AS FRIENDS TOO. I think Ronan would stab Adam in the eye, still. But you know, every friendship has their rough patches.<br />RONAN: I LOVE RONAN SO MUCH HE IS MY FAVOURITE. He is so ferocious and such a giant jerk...but adorable. And so full of secrets. I kind of guessed that (view spoiler) Ronan makes himself so difficult but he really really needs the others. SO BADLY.<br />NOAH: We're losing Noah. I am terrified. He's going a little more crazy as a ghost and I really really really want htem to fix him because I love Noah.<br /><br />Basically I love everyone. Are you shocked. HAH AH. No you're not.<br /><br />The writing is as beautiful as always. I think this is the fastest moving book of the 3 so far! There's a lot of scenery changes. There's villainous action. There's cursed caves and Jesse Dittley. <br /><br />AND I AM SO IN NEED OF BOOK 4 BEFORE I EXPLODE, OKAY???!!<br />description<br /><br />FAVOURITEST QUOTES:<br /><br />"You can just be friends with people, you know," Orla said. "I think it's crazy how you're in love with all those raven boys."<br /><br />*<br /><br />It was true that Blue was just shy of five feet and it was also true that she hadn't eaten her greens, but she'd done the research and she didn't think the two were related.<br /><br />*<br /><br />As they moved through the old barn, Adam felt Ronan's eyes glance off him and away, his disinterest practised but incomplete. Adam wondered if anyone else noticed. Part of him wished they did and immediately felt bad, because it was vanity, really: See, Adam Parrish is wantable, worthy of a crush, not just by anyone, someone like Ronan, who could want Gansey or anyone else and chose Adam for his hungry eyes. <br />Maybe he was wrong. He could be wrong. <br />I am unknowable, Ronan Lynch.<br />(pg. 158)<br /><br />*<br /><br />"YOUR DEAD FRIEND," Jesse noted, sitting down opposite her at the tiny drop-leaf table. The mirror lay between them, face down. <br />"That's not his fault. Why didn't you say you could see him?"<br />"I DIDN'T SAY I COULD SEE YOU, EITHER."<br />"But I'm not dead," Blue pointed out.<br />"BUT YOU ARE PRETTY SHORT."<br />(pg. 183)<br /><br />*<br /><br />She lay there and told herself to go back to sleep, but instead, she got angrier. She was tired of Persephone and Calla and her mother withholding information because Blue wasn't psychic. Of not being able to daydream of fancy colleges because she wasn't rich. Of not being able to hold Gansey's hand because they couldn't hurt Adam's feelings and not being able to kiss Gansey's mouth because she didn't want to kill him. She was tired of knowing that he was going to die and being afraid that her mother would, too. (pg. 196)<br /><br />*<br /><br />Ronan pointed at the cart. "Get in there."<br />"What?"<br />He just continued pointing. <br />Adam said, "Give me a break. This is a public parking lot."<br />"Don't make this ugly, Parrish."<br />As an old lady headed past them, Adam sighed and climbed into the basket of the shopping cart. He drew his knees up so that he would fit. He was full of the knowledge that this was probably going to end with scabs. <br />Ronan gripped the handle with the skittish concentration of a motorcycle racer and eyed the line between them and the BMW parked on the far side of the lot. "What do you think the grade is on this parking lot?"<br />"C plus, maybe a B. Oh. I don't know. Ten degrees?" Adam held the sides of the cart and then thought better of it. He held himself instead. <br />With a savage smile, Ronan shoved the cart off the kerb and belted towards the BMW. As they picked up speed, Ronan called out a joyful and awful swear and then jumped on to the back of the cart himself. As they hurtled towards the BMW, Adam realised that Ronan, as usual, had no intention of stopping before something bad happened. He cupped a hand over his nose just as they glanced off the side of the BMW. The unseated cart wobbled once, twice, and then tipped catastrophically on to its side. It kept skidding, the boys skidding along with it. <br />The three of them came to a stop. <br />"Oh, God," Adam said, touching the road burn on his elbow. It wasn't that bad, really. "God, God. I can feel my teeth."<br />Ronan lay on his back a few feet away. A box of toothpaste rested on his chest and the cart kneeled beside him. He looked profoundly happy. <br />(pg. 233)<br /><br />*<br /><br />"What do we do now?" Gansey asked.<br />From the other room, Calla bellowed, "GO BUY US PIZZA. WITH EXTRA CHEESE, RICHIE RICH."<br />Blue said, "I think she's starting to like you." (pg. 243)<br /><br />* <br /><br />Behind him, he heard Ronan say, "I like the way you losers thought Instagram before first aid. Fuck off." (pg. 288)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12074823462857875587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer16427545596439658425"><b>
  <i>“Mornings like this one were made for memories.” </i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517335704i/24968610.jpg' width='500' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Isn't it the most obscure and abnormal concept that a book filled with random sequences of the alphabet put together to make some sense, can act as a catalyst to generate a chemistry lab full of emotions? <br/>Essentially, you could have an infinite amount of books with the same character count as an airline flight safety manual, but those random string of words put together in just a handful of books can make you <i>feel </i>so intensely. <br/><br/><i>This is what Th</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText16427545596439658425" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“Mornings like this one were made for memories.” </i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517335704i/24968610.jpg" width="500" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Isn't it the most obscure and abnormal concept that a book filled with random sequences of the alphabet put together to make some sense, can act as a catalyst to generate a chemistry lab full of emotions? <br>Essentially, you could have an infinite amount of books with the same character count as an airline flight safety manual, but those random string of words put together in just a handful of books can make you <i>feel </i>so intensely. <br><br><i>This is what The Raven Cycle does. <br>There should be a damn warning label on the cover that should inform your heart to proceed with caution. </i></b><br>_______________<br><br><u>Note: </u>All rights belong to the different artists that have created the (fucking amazing) fanart attached to this review. <br><u>Another Note: </u>This review is broken down with different aspects of tarot cards - linked to different aspects of the book. <br><br><u>
  <b>The King</b>
</u><br><br><i>Kings are considered to be the most mature of the Court Cards. They have travelled through life successfully and are now at the pinnacle of experience and understanding. Thus, the Kings represent the fully developed personalities of each of the Suits.</i><br><br>Each and every character in this series, can have a way to cut your most vital organs up and still make you beg them to stick around because that's just how addictive they are. I'm talking even the villains, the supposed to be villains, the princesses (Ronan.. don't even try and fight me on this), the knights, the supernatural, the heroes, the kings... <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517337803i/24968832.jpg" width="500" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517337803i/24968833.jpg" width="500" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You're going to read this and finish it and then envy anyone else that has the ability to experience these wondrous personalities for the first time again. <br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Let’s leave her,” Ronan said. Gansey replied, “If we abandoned people in caves because they were crazy, you’d still be back in Cabeswater.” </blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><br><br><u>
  <b>The Mirror</b>
</u><br><br><i>The High Priestess symbolizes intuition, psychic energy, the dream world, the unconscious, feelings, instincts and emotions. She senses what is going on below the surface. She is a receptive <b>mirror.</b></i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517337803i/24968834._SY540_.jpg" width="500" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I think what I loved was the fact that everything was practically a freakshow. I love that we were constantly surrounded by surreal aspects and dream things. It took away from reality but let us stay in a real world at the same time. So cheers, Stiefvater. You got me all kinds of fucked up. <br>300 Fox Way and it's residents will forever be a love of mine, and although the plot of the story (personally) is very character driven - we get so many 'paranormal' facets that makes the whole story fly off the pages. <br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>"Why does terror grow so much better away from the sun"</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517337803i/24968835.jpg" width="500" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><u>
  <b>The Magician</b>
</u><br><br><i>The first trump or Major Arcana card in most traditional Tarot decks. ... In divination it is considered by some to succeed The Fool card. He is the middle ground. </i><br><br>Although there were definitely some problems I came across (hence not enabling the five star rating) It was very easily covered up with the humor and banter in between the chaos of everything that was going on. We got the boys being boys, we saw how each of the gang is slowly growing up and on, we get to witness them falling in love etc. etc. <br><br>I loved the chemistry we got with Adam and Ronan in this edition, not to mention Blue and Gansey have been a ship from day one - so the progress with them makes my heart happy. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517337803i/24968836._SY540_.jpg" width="500" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ronan will always be my problematic fave.<br>Adam my chaotic neutral. <br>Gansey, my mother of four. <br>Blue - a hardass, badass, smartass cupcake. <br>And Noah... Noah can't be described because I love him so much. <br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“We are going so slow," Noah said, craning his neck to observe the inevitable queue behind them. "I think I just saw a tricycle pass us.” </blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517337803i/24968837._SY540_.jpg" width="500" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>

    <blockquote>“I think it's crazy how you're in love with all those raven boys.”</blockquote>
  </b>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1809050662" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1809050662" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1809050662?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781407136639" href="/book/show/22978079-blue-lily-lily-blue">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Petrik by: </span>
      Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1809050662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11086148245170491495"><b>You might want to underestimate this 4 stars rating slightly.</b><br/><br/>The Raven Cycle continues to improve with each installment and this is literally the first time I ever gave a 4 star rating to a YA book as I’m not a fan of the genre. Blue Lily, Lily Blue <i>(BLLB)</i> will probably be an easy 5 stars read for those of you who have no qualm with the genre in general.<br/><br/>One of the problems I had with 'The Dream Thieves' was that I feel like that there’s a lack of satisfaction in the sense of plot progression to </span>
  <span id="freeText11086148245170491495" style="display:none"><b>You might want to underestimate this 4 stars rating slightly.</b><br /><br />The Raven Cycle continues to improve with each installment and this is literally the first time I ever gave a 4 star rating to a YA book as I’m not a fan of the genre. Blue Lily, Lily Blue <i>(BLLB)</i> will probably be an easy 5 stars read for those of you who have no qualm with the genre in general.<br /><br />One of the problems I had with 'The Dream Thieves' was that I feel like that there’s a lack of satisfaction in the sense of plot progression to the main plot in exchange for full characterization. This problem is completely unfound here. After establishing the characters background, personality and relationships for the past two books, the plot can finally move on in a well-paced manner. The main characters are back in full focus on their hunt for Owen Glendower, the sleeping Welsh king and there are some captivating twists and turns with some tensions in the plot that were long needed for the series to be better and I enjoyed every moment of it.<br /><br />Something you should know is that although I enjoyed the plot of the series, I do think the plot can be too complex for the audience it catered to. The plot is actually quite complex on the borderline between new adult and adult urban fantasy, it’s definitely not what the fandom led you to believe that this series will be all lovey-dovey romance series with all the shipping of the characters. Don’t believe me? Check out the reviews on GR, you’ll see a lot of 5 stars reviews that stated <b>“I don’t even understand the plot”</b> and yet still gave it 5 stars because their characters ‘shipping’ still sails. I’m not here to judge other ratings at all, people have different criteria on the books they read, my point is to tell you that there is a deep plot here for NA and even adult audience to enjoy. However, in the end, there’s no doubt that this series main strength still lies in the characterization and Maggie’s prose.<br /><br />Remember what I said in my previous review that Ronan Lynch is one of the most well-written character in the entire YA genre? Well, that’s still true but you know what? There’s another addition here, Adam Parrish. I’ll be honest, I didn’t like Adam, his unnecessary angst and pride that never wanted to accept anyone’s help pissed me off. This is why he had the most potential for great character developments and Maggie completely delivered on this. <b>Adam's character development in BLLB is one of the best strength of the book.</b><br /><br />It’s not only Adam though, the buildup to everything that shaped the friendship between all the main characters since the first book took a fruition here. <b>The friendship between Blue and The Raven Boys is the most realistic friendship I ever read in any YA books.</b> They’re realistic, beautiful, and somehow, they remind me of the times I had with my friends in high school. <i>(The supernatural aspect being only the infamous school ghosts stories though.)</i><br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Blue was perfectly aware that it was possible to have a friendship that wasn’t all-encompassing, that wasn’t blinding, deafening, maddening, quickening. It was just that now that she’d had this kind, she didn’t want the other.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />At this point, you should know by now that Maggie’s prose is lyrical, easy and beautiful to read. I’m delighted to find that her prose improvement doesn’t stop there; it keeps on getting better with each installment. I truly believe that her prose is what truly makes this series works; she knows how to write characters realistically. Imo, what she did to this series as what Night Circus by Erin Morgenstern should’ve been <i>(except that this series does have a plot unlike that black and white tent.)</i><br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"Maybe it was good that the world forgot every lesson, every good and bad memory, every triumph and failure, all of it dying with each generation. Perhaps this cultural amnesia spared them all. Perhaps if they remembered everything, hope would die instead."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />The only minor con I had with the book is that Blue’s indecision and attitude in making up her mind can be infuriating to read sometimes. Don’t get me wrong, as I mentioned before, her thoughts and anger, as incoherent and illogical as they are is actually very realistic but at the same time, seeing her repeat them can be tiring.<br /><br /><b>BLLB is the best entry in the series so far and it has set up everything it needs for the conclusion.</b> It has proven itself to me that there’s still a gem to be found in this desert of horrible overhyped series like 'Shade of Magic'. However, for me, it all comes down to the last book of the series on whether Maggie could deliver the conclusion the series deserves to see whether the series truly deserves the hype and praises it gets and I’m going to find out about it now.<br /><br /><i>This review is also featured on <a href="https://booksprens.wordpress.com/reviews/guests-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Booksprens</a><a></a> where I'll be a guest reviewer for this series, check it out! :)</i><br /><br /><i>You can find the rest of my Adult Epic/High Fantasy &amp; Sci-Fi reviews at <a>BookNest</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11086148245170491495" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1944004076" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1944004076" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1944004076?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=couples-i-love">couples-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=memorable-male-characters">memorable-male-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=favorite-female-characters">favorite-female-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=deserves-the-hype">deserves-the-hype</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1944004076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5445324465484683336"><b> 5 Stars </b><br/><br/><b>Overview: Re-Read</b><br/><br/>Umm... I don't have more to add except that I love this book and it's one of my all-time favorites? I appreciate so much more this time around and all of these characters are phenomenal.<br/><br/>Except Cheng, who exists here only to set his character up for the next book. And Maura, who continues to make bad decisions always.<br/><br/><b>Original Review</b> <br/><br/>Here’s the thing with this series. The plot is… <i>odd</i>. <br/><br/>You open the first book expecting something about prep-school boys and maybe ghosts but</span>
  <span id="freeText5445324465484683336" style="display:none"><b> 5 Stars </b><br><br><b>Overview: Re-Read</b><br><br>Umm... I don't have more to add except that I love this book and it's one of my all-time favorites? I appreciate so much more this time around and all of these characters are phenomenal.<br><br>Except Cheng, who exists here only to set his character up for the next book. And Maura, who continues to make bad decisions always.<br><br><b>Original Review</b> <br><br>Here’s the thing with this series. The plot is… <i>odd</i>. <br><br>You open the first book expecting something about prep-school boys and maybe ghosts but then there’s magical trees and an expedition for a dead Welsh King. <br><br> (Or at least, I did.)<br><br>It’s definitely original and exciting—but it’s still <i>odd.</i> Somehow, despite how abstract and engrossing the plot points are, it doesn’t feel like the focus of the story. Instead, it’s the <i>characters</i>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490246829i/22294247._SY540_.jpg" width="280" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(Actual convo I had with my friend tonight. I think he’s starting to get it.) <br><br>The character development here was as nuanced as it was subtle. We’ve all heard about <a href="https://www.autocrit.com/editing/support/showing-vs-telling-indicators/" rel="nofollow noopener">"showing vs telling</a> and this book handles this <i>masterfully.</i> <br><br>At no point are we told “Character A is doing this because of X.” Instead, Steifvater understands her readers are smart enough to pick up on the character motivation if she <i>shows</i> it well. We’re given wonderful insights into the character’s heads, but we are never just <i>told.</i> <br><br>I don’t understand people who claim this book is a ‘filler.’ The <i>sheer</i> amount of development here was phenomenal. <br><br><b>Adam</b><br><i>
  <blockquote>”He left bloody fingerprints on the rock, but there was something satisfying about that. I was here. I exist. I’m alive, because I bleed.”</blockquote>
</i><br><br>-	Arguably has the most development of anyone.<br><br>-	Still my fav &lt;3<br><br>-	There such a focus on him finding <i>balance.</i> With Cabeswater. With his friends. With himself. AND IT'S GREAT.<br><br>-	He becomes so aware of his own agency here and I’m just so proud because he DESERVES happiness okay?<br><br><b>Ronan</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Adam was beginning to realize that he hadn't known Ronan at all. Or rather, he had known part of him and assumed it was all of him.” </i>
</blockquote><br><br>-	Literally made me cry. <br><br>-	Like he thinks and feels with this <i>intensity</i> and it was captivating. Before I knew it I was crying witnessing what he pulls out of his dreams.<br><br>-	Jesus this boy is crushing haaaarrrrrddddd.<br><br>-	(I ship it so much omfg) <br><br>-	The image of Ronan curled up with that blue blanket at The Barns is so poignant and just beautifully done.<br><br><br><b>Blue</b><br><i>
  <blockquote>“It was amazing that she and Ronan didn’t get along better, because they were different brands of the same impossible stuff.” </blockquote>
</i><br><br>-	So let’s talk about this firecracker for a second, shall we? <br><br>-	She is 200%, absolutely, completely flawed.<br><br>-	She overreacts. She’s rude. She can be insensitive without realizing it. <i>Flaws. </i><br><br>-	But she feels <i>real.</i> <br><br>- I don’t need perfect characters. None of the others are perfect either, and Blue shouldn’t be held to a higher standard.<br><br>-	She’s still super frustrating, but well-written.<br><br><b>Gansey</b><br><br><i>
  <blockquote>““I don’t know what I’ll do if I find him, Noah. I don’t know what I’ll be if I’m not looking for him. I don’t know the first thing about how to be that person again.” </blockquote>
</i><br><br>-	These freaking hornets. <br><br>-	Gansey’s whole arc this book revolves around fear and how it factors into his identify and it was GREAT<br><br>-	I’m so envious of his social skills, but also incredibly intimated. <br><br>-	Still a larger-than life hero, but he’s aware of it?<br><br>-	I actually love that he and Blue have their whole moral dilemma here. But I am 100% Team: No More Pain for Adam, but the whole plot really humanizes Gansey quite a bit. It’s fascinating to watch him struggle with something. <br><br>-	That sexy handholding tho.<br><br><b>Others</b><br><br>-	I don't understand any of Maura's decisions. Ever. <br><br>-	Calla and Persphone were expanded upon so much more in this volume! They really became their own individuals, and it was very interesting to see how they functioned together and with Maura. <br><br>-	Will Gwenlillian make more sense later? Because she was suppppeerr random here. What is the deal with the singing?<br><br>-	Henry Cheng seems to exist here primarily to set him up for the next book, and I’m not sure what to think. He seems… scattered? <br><br>-	This narrative is so… aware? I don’t have a better way to describe it. But it feels aware of so much. The fact that all these friendships are borderline-codependent <i>isn’t glossed over.</i> Self-proclaimed feminist Blue addresses characters who feel her ‘story’ didn’t start until she met the boys. It just feels acutely aware of the audience without being shaped by it?<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“I think it's crazy how you're in love with all those raven boys."</blockquote>
</i><br><br>Again. Same.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5445324465484683336" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2060871227827988372"><i>“There was something unfamiliar about him. Something ferocious about his eyes, some sort of bite in his faint smile. Something altogether hectic and unsettled. She stood on the ledge of his smile and looked over the edge.”</i><br/><br/>Even though I always feel like I don't understand a thing that is going on in those books, they are just beautiful. Maybe exactly because I don't understand a thing: They always surprise me, I never know what to expect next but I am never let down.<br/><br/>I think this third installment</span>
  <span id="freeText2060871227827988372" style="display:none"><i>“There was something unfamiliar about him. Something ferocious about his eyes, some sort of bite in his faint smile. Something altogether hectic and unsettled. She stood on the ledge of his smile and looked over the edge.”</i><br /><br />Even though I always feel like I don't understand a thing that is going on in those books, they are just beautiful. Maybe exactly because I don't understand a thing: They always surprise me, I never know what to expect next but I am never let down.<br /><br />I think this third installment was the best so far. I love to see the friendships and more-than-friendships grow. I really hope that Ronan and Adam are going to be a thing! Though I still think that Ronan is an asshole, he just makes me angry...<br />And wow what this book made to my heart! I don't know what was stronger: my love for the characters or my fear they would die. Because Lord I was bloody scared! Worse than any horror movie. Imagination is a strong thing.<br /><br />The books are not perfect but they have this incredible atmosphere of mystery and magic, danger and adventure that make me adore Maggie Stiefvater as an author.<br /><br /> <a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a><br /></span>

<div id="review_1868122409" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1868122409" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1868122409?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=the-best-of-the-best">the-best-of-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=otp">otp</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=found-families">found-families</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1868122409" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5146998247724673941"><blockquote>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1858462459' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Raven Boys</a> ★★★★★ <br/>#2 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1987182325' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dream Thieves</a> ★★★★★<br/>#3 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1868122409' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blue Lily, Lily Blue</a> ★★★★★<br/>#4 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1837779500' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Raven King</a> ★★★★★<br/>#4.5 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2311292720' rel='nofollow noopener'>Opal</a> ★★★★★</blockquote> <br/><blockquote>
  <i>Blue was perfectly aware that it was possible to have a friendship that wasn’t all-encompassing, that wasn’t blinding, deafening, maddening, quickening. It was just that now that she’d had this kind, she didn’t want the other.</i>
</blockquote><br/>Where do I even begin? This review took me six weeks to write, and it's literally only because I loved it so much that I don't know how to describe it. </span>
  <span id="freeText5146998247724673941" style="display:none"><blockquote>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1858462459" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven Boys</a> ★★★★★ <br />#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1987182325" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dream Thieves</a> ★★★★★<br />#3 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1868122409" rel="nofollow noopener">Blue Lily, Lily Blue</a> ★★★★★<br />#4 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1837779500" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven King</a> ★★★★★<br />#4.5 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2311292720" rel="nofollow noopener">Opal</a> ★★★★★</blockquote> <br /><blockquote>
  <i>Blue was perfectly aware that it was possible to have a friendship that wasn’t all-encompassing, that wasn’t blinding, deafening, maddening, quickening. It was just that now that she’d had this kind, she didn’t want the other.</i>
</blockquote><br />Where do I even begin? This review took me six weeks to write, and it's literally only because I loved it so much that I don't know how to describe it. I went through <i>three sleeves</i> of page tabs on this book, and if that doesn't tell you something... I swear, Maggie has created the single most lovable set of characters I have ever met in my entire life. They're all incredible in their own wholly unique way, and their story is just... perfection.<br /><br /><b>Spoilers for books 1 &amp; 2 ahead. And, yes, I am going to gush through this entire review. This is your last warning.</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"I'm glad you misdialed."<br /><br />"Well. Easy mistake to make," she said. "Might do it again."</i>
</blockquote><br />→ <b>Blue Sargent</b> ←<br />I have met so many people who wholly dislike Blue as a character, and I don't know if I'll ever live long enough to understand why. I adore her. She's smart, and brave, and angry, and sad, and flawed, and snarky, and more than anything, she loves with her entire being. Despite her odd upbringing and the way her life differs so greatly from that of most of the Aglionby boys, I feel that she would ultimately give anything to keep them and her family safe.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Ronan had not seen; Adam was still sleeping. The only casualty was his pulse.</i>
</blockquote><br />→ <b>Richard "Dick" Gansey, III</b> ←<br />Where do I even start with Gansey? He's been my favorite Raven Boy from the beginning, and it remains the same; he is so well-intended, so caring and doting, so desperate for something more than the falsehoods and politics of his family. He puts his foot in his mouth constantly, but this book has the best examples so far of how much he loves his friends and the lengths he would happily go to for them, whether it's terror-filled drives in the countryside, looking for Blue, or going against Adam's wishes to protect him one more time from his father. Through it all, he just feels so <i>human</i> and <i>genuine</i>, and I swear I would read endless pages, filled with nothing more than Gansey's inner musings on his loved ones.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>The only thing more pleasing than seeing Ronan singled out was seeing him singled out and forced to repeatedly sing an Irish jig. “Piss up a rope,” Ronan said. Gansey, unoffended, waited. Ronan shook his head, but then, with a wicked smile, he began to sing, “Squash one, squash two, s—”</i>
</blockquote><br />→ <b>Ronan Lynch</b> ←<br />Regarding the last paragraph, if there is one character in this series who can rival my love for Gansey, it's Ronan Lynch. God, I love everything about his angry, moody, fierce little tattooed self. I love how incredibly torn he is between hating himself or hating the world. I love his quiet kindnesses for Adam, and the hints he uses to let his feelings shine through the rage. I love his dedication to Gansey. I love how alike he and Blue are, despite how much they might want to deny it. And I love his stupid <i>squash one, squash two</i> ridiculousness.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>As they moved through the old barn, Adam felt Ronan’s eyes glance off him and away, his disinterest practiced but incomplete. Adam wondered if anyone else noticed. Part of him wished they did and immediately felt bad, because it was vanity, really:<br /><br />'See, Adam Parrish is wantable, worthy of a crush, not just by anyone, someone like Ronan, who could want Gansey or anyone else and chose Adam for his hungry eyes.'</i>
</blockquote><br />→ <b>Adam Parrish</b> ←<br />Oh, sweet, tortured little Adam. I loved him in <i>The Raven Boys</i>, yet found myself endless frustrated by him in <i>The Dream Thieves</i>. This book, though, brought him rushing back into my heart. I felt like I was seeing his true self again, and more than anything, I adored his moments with Ronan, in which he slowly came to realize and accept the feelings that Ronan was presenting him with through this little acts of generosity and emotional connection.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“We are going so slow,” Noah said, craning his neck to observe the inevitable queue behind them. “I think I just saw a tricycle pass us.”</i>
</blockquote><br />→ <b>Noah Czerny</b> ←<br />Noah is, as always, precious, pitiable, and lovable all the same, but this book was the first time that he came across as what he is: a dead, mysterious, and slightly scary thing. I felt so sorry for him as he was subjected to the horrors of possession, and for the first time since midway through book 1, I found myself worried that we were going to lose him before the series ends. I love his friendship with Blue and how comforting his presence is for her, even without the physicality of it.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I think it's crazy how you're in love with all those raven boys.”</i>
</blockquote><br />→ <b>relationships</b> ←<br />I felt like I was going to literally experience spontaneous combustion during this book, because I am so ridiculously hooked on these two blooming romances, and how they contrast each other. On the one hand, you have Ronan and Adam, who have every opportunity in the world to be together, but don't know how to put their feelings into words; on the other hand, you have Gansey and Blue, baring their souls to each other in late night phone calls and car drives, desperately trying not to reach for the forbidden fruit. I don't know if my heart can take much more. ❤<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Adam understood, then, that Gansey and Blue’s awe changed this place. Ronan and Adam may have seen this place as magical, but Gansey and Blue’s wonder made it holy.</i>
</blockquote><br />→ <b>plot twists &amp; turns</b> ←<br />Okay, I'm done gushing about the characters. Moving on to the <i>plot</i>, I thought this book has the most captivating story line of all three so far. It was incredibly suspenseful with Blue's missing mother, and there were some side character moments that broke my heart so much more thoroughly than I thought they ever could have, but anyone who found themselves frustrated with the focus on characters in previous installments would probably be delighted by the non-stop action and scheming in this one.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Mornings like this one were made for memories.</i>
</blockquote><br />→ <b>final thoughts</b> ←<br />My final thoughts for this book are the same as they were for the last two: if you haven't read this series, you're missing out on an amazing experience. These characters are so wonderful, and the world of Henrietta and Cabeswater is a phenomenon that everyone should witness. I cannot recommend this series enough. It has so quickly become one of my all-time favorites, and I am only sad to know that it's almost over.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5146998247724673941" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Shambhawi P." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8936537-shambhawi-p"><img alt="Shambhawi P." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442655888p2/8936537.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/717581867?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shambhawi P." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shambhawi P." href="/user/show/8936537-shambhawi-p">Shambhawi P.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8936537-shambhawi-p?shelf=arc">arc</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer717581867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8289420299199665141"><b>
  <u>×××May contain minor spoilers×××</u>
</b><br/><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>"Queens and kings<br/>Kings and queens<br/>Blue lily, lily blue<br/>Crowns and birds<br/>Swords and things<br/>Blue lily, lily blue"</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br/>This book is nothing like I expected. This book was everything I wanted it to be. The book gave me chills, it broke my heart. It made me laugh, it made me mad. It made me crazy. It made me cry - not a lot, not as much as The Raven Boys or The Dream Thieves but little silent tears pooling up in my eyes.<br/><br/>This book, at parts, made me forget that R</span>
  <span id="freeText8289420299199665141" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>×××May contain minor spoilers×××</u>
</b><br /><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>"Queens and kings<br />Kings and queens<br />Blue lily, lily blue<br />Crowns and birds<br />Swords and things<br />Blue lily, lily blue"</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br />This book is nothing like I expected. This book was everything I wanted it to be. The book gave me chills, it broke my heart. It made me laugh, it made me mad. It made me crazy. It made me cry - not a lot, not as much as The Raven Boys or The Dream Thieves but little silent tears pooling up in my eyes.<br /><br />This book, at parts, made me forget that Richard Campbell Gansey was going to die. Until something or the other would would violently remind me of that.<br /><b>
  <blockquote>"Blue", he warned, but his voice was chaotic. This close, his throat was scented with mint and wool sweater and vinyl car seat, and Gansey, just Gansey.<br />She said, "I just want to pretend. I want to pretend that I could."<br />He breathed out.<br />What was a kiss without a kiss?</blockquote>
</b><br />This book had more Gansey x Blue moments in it. They were powerful moments with so many emotions that where nothing happens but both their feelings are laid bare for our inspection. And they touched me.<br /><br />And we have Adam. Poor, broken, stupid, proud Adam who promised himself to Cabeswater and is paying the due of his sacrifice. Adam who is in the middle of a lawsuit against his father. Adam who is doing school, after school jobs, realizing that Blue might not be for him after all, letting go of his stupidity a little at a time by realizing that letting Gansey be his friend is not necessarily being beholden to Gansey. Adam whom I hate a little less now. Adam who is the Magician of this quest for the sleeping king.<br /><br />We see a different side of Adam and Ronan's friendship in this book in light of the knowledge of Ronan's crush. It's sweet how much they fight and how much they disagree and how much Adam has guessed and how much of his real feelings is Ronan ready to show. It's sweet and slow and adorable and even though I am not sure whether Ronan x Adam is going to be a thing yet, it's a beautiful friendship nonetheless. <i>I totally ship them.</i><br /><br />There is a lot happening in this book even if it is shorter than the other two. We have Maura who has run off to look for Butternut after leaving a cryptic note. We also have one not so new and one new character in Colin Greenmantle and his wife Piper who have come to Henrietta for reasons. We have Jesse Dittley - another someone whom Neeve saw and Blue wrote in the night when Blue had first seen Gansey. We have the mysterious cave and mysterious tombs and cryptic messages. And more sleepers.<br /><br />But most of all this is a book about friendship between the five different people and how they all work so well together. They are closer to Glendower now than they ever were and closer to the climax and if all goes as foretold Gansey's death. <del>I wish I did not know it was going to happen at all.</del><br /><br /><b>4.5 Stars</b> <br />2015 is too faraway.<br /><br /><i> This ARC was provided to me by the publishers in exchange of an honest review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8289420299199665141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1826315881" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1826315881" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1826315881?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2016">z-faves2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-coverporn">z-coverporn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-rereads">x-rereads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-series">x-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=identity">identity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2016">z-read2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1826315881" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2486719305494844607">me when someone I know hates on Adam Parrish:<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534677525i/26154892.jpg' width='400' height='350' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>[we'll talk about my favorite fictional character of all time........... later in this review but for now have a meme]<br/><br/>Okay, so this was a <i>fantastic</i> middle book. <i>Blue Lily Lily Blue</i> is a totally different beast than the <i>Dream Thieves</i>, but it's <i>so good</i>. Even thinking about this book makes me... so happy. I think what's funny about this series is I keep having problems with it but I'm okay with it - these books are as messy as life, as fucked up and emot</span>
  <span id="freeText2486719305494844607" style="display:none">me when someone I know hates on Adam Parrish:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534677525i/26154892.jpg" width="400" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>[we'll talk about my favorite fictional character of all time........... later in this review but for now have a meme]<br><br>Okay, so this was a <i>fantastic</i> middle book. <i>Blue Lily Lily Blue</i> is a totally different beast than the <i>Dream Thieves</i>, but it's <i>so good</i>. Even thinking about this book makes me... so happy. I think what's funny about this series is I keep having problems with it but I'm okay with it - these books are as messy as life, as fucked up and emotionally charged and full of errors that won't ever be resolved. As I've said in my reviews for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1822328079" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven Boys</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1825674919?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dream Thieves</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1826315881?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Blue Lily, Lily Blue</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1827604862?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven King</a>, I love all of these characters so much, on a level of my soul that most fictional characters do not touch. Because these books are genuinely magic.<br><br><i>
  <b>→why am I bitter?←</b>
</i><br>I will be very honest and say I think these books deserve praise for characters, not plot. The plot of <i>Blue Lily, Lily Blue</i>, specifically was... eh? What happened in this book? Because I'm genuinely not sure I know. And yeah, some of that is Maggie's trademark style. But there wasn't not much tension because I never knew what the fuck was happening. Confusing, magical-realism-esque plot is Maggie's trademark. Apparently. I will also say that Ronan never narrated chapters, and that really did sadden me, because he has such a distinct narrative style from Gansey and Adam and Blue! Sad. <br><br>Also, <b>Blue and Gansey still aren't progressing as characters</b>. Give them the character development they deserve.<br><br><i>
  <b>→why am I in love?←</b>
</i><br>So first of all, adorable scenes with the #squad always get me going. I especially loved the courtroom scene. I want a friend group like the raven squad. Without the dead Welsh kings and excess testosterone, maybe.<br><br>In general, I think this book is one of the best in the series for all the relationships. There is so much fantastic relationship building in this book. Blue and Gansey's relationship makes me more emotional by the minute. I care about Gansey and Adam's vaguely gay friendship so much. I am physically hurt inside by Ronan and Blue being bros.<br><br>And I like to die!<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Ronan knew Adam, but Adam wasn't sure he knew Ronan at all.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Also, side note, I stand by every update I made about this book.<br><br><i>
  <b>→why am I dead inside?←</b>
</i><br>Uh, um, so there’s a character in this book that - <i>literally</i> - has my personality. So I want to talk about that. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Why did he care if Gansey and Ronan saw this? <br>They already knew. They knew everything about him. What a lie unknowable was. The only person who didn't know Adam was himself.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>There’s this thing this character does, where he is one of the most Outwardly Stable members of his friend group, and he is also going through so much and probably hasn’t slept since 1920, and yet he still manages to come off as a very pragmatic rational person. most of the time. but his internal monologue around himself just fucking drips with emotional tiredness and, below that, this sense of self-loathing. he compartmentalizes his feelings and also lets himself break down. there’s a scene in the third book of this series where he’s interacting with someone in his life who hurt him, so much, and he responds to it by completely dissociating for a full chapter and it read like my inner monologue in that. exact. situation.<br><br>Oh, and he has my flaws. so that’s really fun! I love confessionals.<br><br>he is… incredibly aware of his own flaws and yet completely unwilling to admit flaws, because he is so used to people turning around and throwing them right back in his face. that’s me. he is completely incapable of receiving gifts because he knows that at any moment, they can be thrown back in his face, with him as the ungrateful one. that’s me.<br><br>and he worries, all the time, both subtly and unsubtly, that he is a danger to others, and he is on the verge of becoming his parents. his entire character arc is based around him realizing he isn’t. and that was so fucking painful and so fucking relatable and I don’t know how to handle it.<br><br>His constant self-awareness, his self destructive ambition, his confidence contrasting with his self-doubt. every chapter he narrates felt like someone had come into my home and stolen my obscure thought processes and I hate it and I am so. invested. in it.<br><br>This series is so genuine and human. And I am so glad I read it.<br><br><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2486719305494844607" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-ya-and-fantasy">fave-ya-and-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1056789183" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12435259769610899498"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459370498i/18603641._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>▒ <b>My ten favorite things about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17378508.Blue_Lily__Lily_Blue__The_Raven_Cycle___3_' title='Blue Lily, Lily Blue (The Raven Cycle, #3) by Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blue Lily, Lily Blue</a></b> ▒<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"Ronan kept going, his voice louder. "No. Do you hear me, Cabeswater? You promised to keep me safe. Who are we to you? Nothing? If you let him die, that is <i>not keeping me safe.</i> Do you understand? If they die, I die, too."</b>
</blockquote><br/>➊ To the surprise of absolutely <i>nobody</i>, <b>Ronan takes the first place hands down</b> even without having any chapter from his point of view. Actually, after the intensity of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17347389.The_Dream_Thieves__The_Raven_Cycle___2_' title='The Dream Thieves (The Raven Cycle, #2) by Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dream Thieves</a>, getting to observe him through othe</span>
  <span id="freeText12435259769610899498" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459370498i/18603641._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>▒ <b>My ten favorite things about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17378508.Blue_Lily__Lily_Blue__The_Raven_Cycle___3_" title="Blue Lily, Lily Blue (The Raven Cycle, #3) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Blue Lily, Lily Blue</a></b> ▒<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Ronan kept going, his voice louder. "No. Do you hear me, Cabeswater? You promised to keep me safe. Who are we to you? Nothing? If you let him die, that is <i>not keeping me safe.</i> Do you understand? If they die, I die, too."</b>
</blockquote><br>➊ To the surprise of absolutely <i>nobody</i>, <b>Ronan takes the first place hands down</b> even without having any chapter from his point of view. Actually, after the intensity of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17347389.The_Dream_Thieves__The_Raven_Cycle___2_" title="The Dream Thieves (The Raven Cycle, #2) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dream Thieves</a>, getting to observe him through other's eyes (who am I kidding : through Adam's) was so so so satisfying. I want more, though. <br><br>➋ <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17378508.Blue_Lily__Lily_Blue__The_Raven_Cycle___3_" title="Blue Lily, Lily Blue (The Raven Cycle, #3) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Blue Lily, Lily Blue</a> will be forever remembered as The Book Where I Finally Love Adam</b>. Shocking, I know, given how much I wanted to slap his whiny ass in the previous books (sorry not sorry). First his evolution is freaking interesting on its own (who doesn't like a Magician with Slytherin-<i>ish</i> potential now tell me? Okaaaay, I might be *a little* subjective. Look at my profile! *waits patiently* <i>Now</i> you get it) and secondly I just can't ignore that 90% of his scenes are shared by The Boy Who Dreams Baby Ravens. Duh.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"With a savage smile, Ronan shoved the cart off the kerb and belted towards the BMW. As they picked up speed, Ronan called out a joyful and awful swear and then jumped on to the back of the cart himself. As they hurtled towards the BMW, Adam realised that Ronan, as usual, had no intention of stopping before something bad happened. He cupped a hand over his nose just as they glanced off the side of the BMW. The unseated cart wobbled once, twice, and then tipped catastrophically on to its side. It kept skidding, the boys skidding along with it.<br>The three of them came to a stop.<br>"Oh, God," Adam said, touching the road burn on his elbow. It wasn't that bad, really. "God, God. I can feel my teeth."<br><b>Ronan lay on his back a few feet away. A box of toothpaste rested on his chest and the cart kneeled beside him. He looked profoundly happy.</b> "</i>
</blockquote><br>➌ I'm gonna throw a <b>PYNCH</b> on there, because I'm redundant like that. Seriously, though. SE-RIOU-SLY. 80% of my favorite quotes are reformulations of something like... <i>meanwhile, Ronan and Adam kept disappearing together</i>.*Almost* every favorite scene stars them : the <i>BARN</i>. The <i>CHURCH</i>. The <i>GROCERY STORE</i>. Oh. My. Gosh. From the shortest looks and grips to the most adorable and heartbreaking interactions, <b>these boys put my heart into overdrive</b>.<br><br>#Can't Compute<br>#I<b>SHIP</b>IT.I<b>SHIP</b>IT.I<b>SHIP</b>IT. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Light, or something like light, reflected off it onto Ronan's chin and cheeks, rendering him stark and handsome and terrifying and someone else. Then he blew on it. His breath passed through the word, the mirror, the unwritten line.<br>Adam heard a whisper in his ear. Something moved and stirred inside him. Ronan's eyelashes fluttered darkly. <br><i>What are we doing -</i>"</b>
</blockquote><br>➍ Granted, we can say what we want about these books, about the confusion of their plots and the true love bits and Mallory's dog (okay sorry dog, that wasn't called for), but <b>the beauty of the relationships pictured will forever make them special for me</b>. The loyalty despite the doubts, the trust - even if sometimes begrudgingly given at first - the support and the BANTER between Blue and her boys is EVERYTHING. Honestly? <b>They're just all kinds of amazing and a little heartbreaking</b>. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Ronan's arms were still locked around her; she felt them quivering. She didn't know if it was from muscle strain or worry. He had not even hesitated before grabbing her.<br><i>I can't let myself forget that.</i>"</b>
</blockquote><br>You better not is the only thing I will say. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"The door cracked open..."</b>
</blockquote><br>You know what I mean, guys. The FEELS. <br><br>➎ ♪ SQUASH ONE, SQUASH TWO, S-♫<br><br>➏ <b>Greenmantle and Piper</b>. <i>Erm-</i> this is the moment I'm supposed to feel bad for loving the villains, right? But-but-b- they're <i>funny!</i> Who am I to resist them tell me? <br><br>➐ JESSE THE YELLER. BECAUSE HIS CURSE IS BADASS TOO. ALSO, I HAVE A SOFT SPOT FOR CHARACTERS WHO USE CAPS. BECAUSE OF REASONS.<br><br>➑ There's nothing better than <b>late night calls</b>, don't you think? (here's the moment 99% of my friends think, FUCKING FINALLY, ANNA! Oops)<br><br>➒ <b>Calla and the <i>Pretty One</i>'s argument</b>. Or is it Richie Rich? I can never remember. <br><br>➓ <b><u>It's official</u> : there's nothing like a <i>Raven Boys</i> reread to make yourself feel a special kind of <i>stupid</i></b>; so many hidden details that came to light, I can't even. Really, though : how in the <i>world</i> did I miss so many things the first time? HOW? Was I high or something? <br><br>Oh, nope. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1330292.Maggie_Stiefvater" title="Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Maggie Stiefvater</a>'s plot is just <b>way more layered and complex</b> than I first imagined. Or, I'm smarter now (somehow I doubt it) (it's been 2 years, not 2 decades)<br><br>Sigh. <b>Now I wait</b>. <br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="12435259769610899498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2069104747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6652993144821771070">Reread update 11/7/19:<br/>This reread solidified that not only is BLLB my favorite book in the series, this is my favorite book of all time. Ever. Ever written. Trying to talk about this book in my reread vlog literally almost made me start crying. YIKES I love it.<br/><br/><br/>Updated review 10/14/17:<br/><br/>I was curious if rereading this series would change my favorite book, but it definitely didn't. I knew from the first couple of chapters that this one just stands out from the rest for me. Maybe it is because it has</span>
  <span id="freeText6652993144821771070" style="display:none">Reread update 11/7/19:<br />This reread solidified that not only is BLLB my favorite book in the series, this is my favorite book of all time. Ever. Ever written. Trying to talk about this book in my reread vlog literally almost made me start crying. YIKES I love it.<br /><br /><br />Updated review 10/14/17:<br /><br />I was curious if rereading this series would change my favorite book, but it definitely didn't. I knew from the first couple of chapters that this one just stands out from the rest for me. Maybe it is because it has the absolute best side characters of the entire series, or because there is moderately less angst than in books 2 or 4, but something about this one speaks to me. <br />I do also think it has to do with the fact that some of my absolute FAVORITE character development happens in this installment. The first time I read this series, this is the first book that made me cry. It is emotional, and you really dig below the surface of every single character and I think that's impressive, considering this is the shortest book of the series. Anyway, I cried again when I read this. I adore it with my whole heart.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1699966185" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17227243473073415345"><b><i>Blue Lily, Lily Blue (RC 03)</i>, by Maggie Stiefvater: 5 “Barrel of Monkeys” Stars.</b><br/><br/><i>“ ‘What’s that slowly phrase?’ Noah asked. ‘Slowly, slowly …’<br/>‘… catchy monkey,’ Gansey finished.” <br/>~ Noah Czerny & Richard Gansey III.</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468683580ra/19736452.gif' width='380' height='210' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>According to the <i>Oxford Dictionary of Proverbs</i></b>, the phrase Noah refers to is actually: <i>Softly, softly, catchee monkey</i>. Basically, it means that in very tricky situations – like catching monkeys – prudence, preparation, and patience are more effective than impulsiveness, irrationality, a</span>
  <span id="freeText17227243473073415345" style="display:none"><b><i>Blue Lily, Lily Blue (RC 03)</i>, by Maggie Stiefvater: 5 “Barrel of Monkeys” Stars.</b><br><br><i>“ ‘What’s that slowly phrase?’ Noah asked. ‘Slowly, slowly …’<br>‘… catchy monkey,’ Gansey finished.” <br>~ Noah Czerny &amp; Richard Gansey III.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468683580ra/19736452.gif" width="380" height="210" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>According to the <i>Oxford Dictionary of Proverbs</i></b>, the phrase Noah refers to is actually: <i>Softly, softly, catchee monkey</i>. Basically, it means that in very tricky situations – like catching monkeys – prudence, preparation, and patience are more effective than impulsiveness, irrationality, and impetuosity. In other words, the characters in Maggie Stiefvater’s Raven Cycle series better stock up on smarts and endurance because all of them have a shit-ton of monkeys to catchee. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468683580ra/19736453.gif" width="380" height="235" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>“I think I miss this part. The beginning. This is the beginning, right? Oh, wait, no, it’s the other one. I forgot. I actually hate this part.” ~ Noah Czerny.</i><br><br><b>If <i>The Dream Thieves (Raven Cycle 02)</i> is about secrets and fears</b>, then <i>Blue Lily, Lily Blue</i> is about endings and beginnings. Before new things can begin, old things must end. Which means: Blue and her psychics must catch Maura. Maura must catch Blue’s father. Ronan and Mr. Grey must catch a very bad man, before a very bad man catches them. And Adam must catch himself. Then, everyone must help Gansey catch Glendower because no one wants Gansey to die. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468683580ra/19736454.gif" width="390" height="210" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> “All I’d like to know is if there is any way to get here from what I’m doing now.” ~ Blue Sargent.</i><br><br><b>While catching specific monkeys will no doubt be hella hard</b>, catching general monkeys will be darn near impossible. Generally speaking, there are some mega ginormous general monkeys in Henrietta and they all want to teach our brave, little group some mega ginormous lessons about life and adulthood (in general), and themselves (in particular). <br><br>And, therein lies another main theme of, <i>The Raven Cycle</i> series. Because:<br><br>TRUTH: There’s <i>always</i> a way to get where you want to go. TRUTH: Getting there <i>will</i> be difficult. TRUTH: If you want to get there bad enough, you’ll <i>find</i> a way. TRUTH: It’s easier if you remember to <i>Softly, softly catchee monkey</i>, because if you take the wrong path, you can always turn around, but it'll take a hell of a lot longer to get where you want to go. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468683580ra/19736455.gif" width="390" height="210" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>“Well, this looks like a barrel of monkeys, pun intended!” ~ Ms. Shiftlet (Blue’s Guidance Councilor).</i><br><br><b>Indeed it does, Ms. Shiftlet!</b> Indeed it does! <br><br>In fact, the whole <i>Raven Cycle</i> series not only <i>looks</i> like a barrel of monkeys, it <i>is</i> a barrel of monkeys, pun intended! But hey! I’ve got one book left to read, so I better quit <i>monkeying</i> around and get to it. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468683580ra/19736456.gif" width="390" height="210" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Blue Lily, Lily Blue (Raven Cycle 03)</i>, by Maggie Stiefvater: 5 “Barrel of Monkeys” Stars.<br><br><b>LINKS TO REVIEWS OF BOOKS 1-2 &amp; 4:</b><br><i>The Raven Boys (RC #1):</i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1692794006?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Click Me Baby!</a><br><i>The Dream Thieves (RC #2):</i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1696306764?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">And Again!</a><br><i>The Raven King (RC #4):</i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1692242580?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">One More Time!</a></span>

But what she didn't realize about Blue and her boys was that they were all in love with one another. She was no less obsessed with them than they were with her, or one another, analyzing every conversation and gesture, drawing out every joke into a longer and longer running gag, spending each moment either with one another or thinking about when next they would be with one another.   </b>
